<center>Back to Top</center>
  Multiple CGT consequences for the same down interest or up interest

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A <sup>*</sup>down interest or <sup>*</sup>up interest of which you are an

<sup>*</sup>affected owner may be covered by 2 or more items in the table in

subsection 725-250(2).</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>If the <sup>*</sup>cost base or <sup>*</sup>reduced cost base of the same <sup>*</sup>down interest or <sup>*</sup>up interest is decreased or uplifted under 2 or more items, it is decreased or uplifted by the total of the amounts worked out under those items.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>If for a particular <sup>*</sup>down interest there is a <sup>*</sup>taxing event generating a gain under an item in the table in section&#160;725-245, that taxing event is in addition to: </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>each taxing event generating a gain for that interest under any other item

in that table; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>each decrease in the <sup>*</sup>cost base or <sup>*</sup>reduced cost

base of the interest under an item in the table in subsection 725-250(2).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Subdivision&#160;725-E&#151;Consequences for down interest or up interest as trading stock or a revenue asset 

Table of sections

725-310	Consequences for down interest or up interest as trading stock
 725-315	_Adjustable value_ of trading stock
 725-320	Consequences for down interest or up interest as a revenue asset
 725-325	_Adjustable value_ of revenue asset
 725-335	How to work out those consequences
 725-340	Multiple trading stock or revenue asset consequences for the same down interest or up interest

725-310  Consequences for down interest or up interest as trading stock

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The consequences of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift for your

<sup>*</sup>trading stock are of one or more of these 3 kinds:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the <sup>*</sup>adjustable values of <sup>*</sup>down interests of which

you are an <sup>*</sup>affected owner are reduced (see subsection&#160;(2));</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the adjustable values of <sup>*</sup>up interests of which you are an

affected owner are uplifted (see subsection&#160;(3));</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>there are one or more <sup>*</sup>taxing events generating a gain for down

interests of which you are an affected owner (see subsection&#160;(5)).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Effect of reduction or uplift of adjustable value_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value of a <sup>*</sup>down interest that is

your trading stock is reduced under section&#160;725-335, you are treated as if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd><sup>*</sup>immediately before the <sup>*</sup>decrease time, you had sold

the interest to someone else (at <sup>*</sup>arm's length and in the ordinary

course of business) for its <sup>*</sup>adjustable value immediately before the

decrease time; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>immediately after the decrease time, you had bought the interest back for

the reduced adjustable value.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>If the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value of an <sup>*</sup>up interest that is

your <sup>*</sup>trading stock is uplifted under section&#160;725-335, you are

treated as if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd><sup>*</sup>immediately before the <sup>*</sup>increase time, you had sold

the interest to someone else (at <sup>*</sup>arm's length and in the ordinary

course of business) for its <sup>*</sup>adjustable value immediately before the

increase time; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>immediately after the increase time, you had bought the interest back for

the uplifted adjustable value.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>However, the increase in the cost of an <sup>*</sup>up interest because of

paragraph&#160;(3)(b) is taken into account from time to time only to the

extent that the amount of the increase is still reflected in the market value

of the interest.

</dd> </dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	The situations where the increase in cost would be taken

into account include:

 </dl></dl>

*	in working out your deductions for the cost of trading stock acquired during the income year in which the increase time happens; and
 *	the end of an income year if the interest's closing value as trading stock is worked out on the basis of its cost; and
 *	the start of the income year in which the interest is disposed of, if that happens in a later income year and the interest's closing value as trading stock at the end of the previous income year was worked out on the basis of its cost.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

	If the interest stops being trading stock, section&#160;70-110

treats you as having disposed of it.

 </dl></dl>

_Taxing event generating a gain_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>For each <sup>*</sup>taxing event generating a gain under an item in the

table in subsection 725-335(3), the gain is included in your assessable income

for the income year in which the <sup>*</sup>decrease time happens.

</dd> </dl></dl>

725-315  Adjustable value of trading stock

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		If a <sup>*</sup>down interest or <sup>*</sup>up interest is your trading

stock, its _adjustable value_ at a particular time is:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>if the interest has been <sup>*</sup>trading stock of yours ever since the

start of the income year in which that time occurs&#151;its <sup>*</sup>value as

trading stock at the start of the income year; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>otherwise&#151;its cost.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	If an interest has been affected by an earlier direct

value shift during the same income year, it will be treated as having already

been sold and repurchased (because of an earlier application of

section&#160;725-310). As a result, the cost on repurchase becomes its

adjustable value immediately before the decrease time or increase time for the

later direct value shift. Note 2:	The adjustable value of an interest that is an up interest because it was issued at a discount is worked out under paragraph&#160;(b).  </dl></dl>

725-320  Consequences for down interest or up interest as a revenue asset

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The consequences of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift for your

<sup>*</sup>revenue assets are of one or more of these 3 kinds:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the <sup>*</sup>adjustable values of <sup>*</sup>down interests of which

you are an <sup>*</sup>affected owner are reduced (see subsection&#160;(2));</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the adjustable values of <sup>*</sup>up interests of which you are an

affected owner are uplifted (see subsection&#160;(3));</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>one or more <sup>*</sup>taxing events generating a gain for down interests

of which you are an affected owner (see subsection&#160;(5)).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Effect of reduction or uplift of adjustable value_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value of a <sup>*</sup>down interest that is

your <sup>*</sup>revenue asset is decreased under section&#160;725-335, you are

treated as if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd><sup>*</sup>immediately before the <sup>*</sup>decrease time, you had sold

the interest to someone else for its <sup>*</sup>adjustable value immediately

before the decrease time; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>immediately afterwards, you had bought the interest back for the reduced

adjustable value; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>from the time when you bought it back, the interest continued to be a

revenue asset, for the same reasons as it was a revenue asset before you sold

it.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>If the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value of an <sup>*</sup>up interest that is

your <sup>*</sup>revenue asset is uplifted under section&#160;725-335, you are

treated as if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd><sup>*</sup>immediately before the <sup>*</sup>increase time, you had sold

the interest to someone else for its <sup>*</sup>adjustable value immediately

before the increase time; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>immediately afterwards, you had bought the interest back for the uplifted

adjustable value; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>from the time when you bought it back, the interest continued to be a

revenue asset, for the same reasons as it was a revenue asset before you sold

it.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>However, the uplift in <sup>*</sup>adjustable value is taken into account

only to the extent that the amount of the uplift is still reflected in the

market value of the interest when it is disposed of or otherwise realised.

</dd> </dl></dl>

_Taxing event generating a gain_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>For each <sup>*</sup>taxing event generating a gain under an item in the

table in subsection 725-335(3), the gain is included in your assessable income

for the income year in which the <sup>*</sup>decrease time happens.

</dd> </dl></dl>

725-325  Adjustable value of revenue asset

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If a <sup>*</sup>down interest is your <sup>*</sup>revenue asset, its

_adjustable value_ immediately before the <sup>*</sup>decrease time

is the total of the amounts that would be subtracted from the gross disposal

proceeds in calculating any profit or loss on disposal of the interest if you

disposed of it immediately before the decrease time.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>If an <sup>*</sup>up interest is your <sup>*</sup>revenue asset and it increases in market value because of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift, its _adjustable value_ immediately before the <sup>*</sup>increase time is the total of the amounts that would be subtracted from the gross disposal proceeds in calculating any profit or loss on disposal of the interest if you disposed of it immediately before the increase time.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>If an <sup>*</sup>up interest is your <sup>*</sup>revenue asset and it is issued at a <sup>*</sup>discount, it is taken to have an _adjustable value_ immediately before it is issued equal to the consideration paid or given by you for the interest. </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	If an interest has been affected by an earlier direct value

shift during the same income year, it will be treated as having already been

sold and repurchased (because of an earlier application of

section&#160;725-320). As a result, the cost on repurchase becomes its

adjustable value immediately before the decrease time or increase time for the

later direct value shift.

 </dl></dl>

_\[The next section is sectionÂ 725-335.]_

725-335  How to work out those consequences

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>This section sets out the consequences of the <sup>*</sup>direct value

shift for a <sup>*</sup>down interest or <sup>*</sup>up interest as

<sup>*</sup>trading stock or a <sup>*</sup>revenue asset.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>If you have both trading stock and revenue assets, items&#160;1 and 2 of the table in subsection&#160;(3) can apply once to the trading stock and again to the revenue assets. The other items apply (if at all) to the trading stock and revenue assets together. </dd> </dl></dl>

_Decreases and uplifts in adjustable value_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>To the extent that the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift is from

<sup>*</sup>down interests specified in an item in the table to <sup>*</sup>up

interests specified in that item:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value of each of those down interests is

decreased by the amount worked out under the section (if any) specified for the

down interests in the last column of that item; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the adjustable value of each of those <sup>*</sup>up interests is uplifted

by the amount worked out under the section (if any) specified for the up

interests in that column.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>To the extent that the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift is from

<sup>*</sup>down interests:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>of which you are an <sup>*</sup>affected owner; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>that are specified in item&#160;2, 4 or 7 in the table in

subsection&#160;(3);

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

to <sup>*</sup>up interests specified in that item, those up interests give rise to a _taxing event generating a gain_ for you under that item on each of those down interests. The gain is worked out under section&#160;725-365.

725-340  Multiple trading stock or revenue asset consequences for the same down interest or up interest

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A <sup>*</sup>down interest or <sup>*</sup>up interest of which you are an

<sup>*</sup>affected owner may be covered by 2 or more items in the table in

subsection 725-335(3).</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>If the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value of the same <sup>*</sup>down interest or <sup>*</sup>up interest is decreased or uplifted under 2 or more items, it is decreased or uplifted by the total of the amounts worked out under those items.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>If for a particular <sup>*</sup>down interest there is a <sup>*</sup>taxing event generating a gain under an item, that taxing event is in addition to: </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>each taxing event generating a gain for that interest under any other item

in the table; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>each decrease in the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value of the interest under

that or any other item in the table.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

725-365  Decreases in adjustable values of down interests (with pre-shift gains), and taxing events generating a gain

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		Use the following method statement:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to work out the amount of the gain for a <sup>*</sup>taxing event

generating a gain under:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>section&#160;725-245; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>item&#160;2, 4 or 7 of the table in subsection 725-335(3); and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>to work out the decrease in <sup>*</sup>adjustable value of a

<sup>*</sup>down interest under:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>item&#160;1, 2, 3, 4 or 6 of the table in subsection 725-250(2); or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>item&#160;1, 2, 4 or 7 of the table in subsection 725-335(3).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

_Method statement_

_Step 1._	Group together all <sup>*</sup>down interests that:

	(a)	are of the kind referred to in the relevant item; and
 	(b)	immediately before the <sup>*</sup>decrease time, had the same <sup>*</sup>adjustable value as the down interest; and
 	(c)	immediately before that time had the same market value as the down 
<center>Back to Top</center>
 interest; and
 	(d)	sustained the same decrease in market value as the down interest because of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift.

_Step 2_.	Work out the value shifted from that group of <sup>*</sup>down interests to the <sup>*</sup>up interests referred to in the relevant item using the following formula:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1213.gif)</sub>
 _Step 3._	Work out the notional adjustable value of the value shifted from that group of <sup>*</sup>down interests to those <sup>*</sup>up interests using the formula:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1214.gif)</sub>
 _Step 4_.	The decrease in the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value  of the <sup>*</sup>down interest under the relevant item is equal to:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1215.gif)</sub>
 _Step 5_.	For a <sup>*</sup>taxing event generating a gain under the relevant item, the amount of the gain  is equal to:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1216.gif)</sub>

725-370  Uplifts in adjustable values of up interests under certain table items

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		Use the following method statement to work out the uplift in

<sup>*</sup>adjustable value of an <sup>*</sup>up interest under:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>item&#160;1 or 2 of the table in subsection 725-250(2); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>item&#160;1 of the table in subsection 725-335(3).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Method statement_

_Step 1_.	If the market value of the <sup>*</sup>up interest increases because of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift, group together all up interests of the kind referred to in the relevant item that:

	(a)	immediately before the <sup>*</sup>increase time, had the same <sup>*</sup>adjustable value as the up interest; and
 	(b)	sustained the same increase in market value as the up interest because of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift.

	If the <sup>*</sup>up interest is issued at a <sup>*</sup>discount, group together all <sup>*</sup>up interests of the kind referred to in the relevant item that:

	(c)	immediately before the <sup>*</sup>increase time, had the same <sup>*</sup>adjustable value as the up interest; and
 	(d)	because of the direct value shift, are issued at the same discount as the up interest.

_Step 2._ The notional adjustable value of the value shifted from the <sup>*</sup>down interests referred to in the relevant item to all the <sup>*</sup>up interests referred to in that item has already been worked out under one or more applications of step 3 of the method statement in section&#160;725-365.
 _Step 3._ Use the following formula to work out how much of that notional adjustable value is attributable to the value shifted to the group of <sup>*</sup>up interests referred to in step 1 of this method statement:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1217.gif)</sub>
 _Step 4._	The uplift in the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value  of the <sup>*</sup>up interest under the relevant item is equal to:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1218.gif)</sub>

725-375  Uplifts in adjustable values of up interests under other table items

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		Use the following method statement to work out the uplift in

<sup>*</sup>adjustable value of an <sup>*</sup>up interest under:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>item&#160;3, 4, 5 or 8 of the table in subsection 725-250(2); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>item&#160;2, 3, 6 or 9 of the table in subsection 725-335(3).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Method statement_

_Step 1_.	If the market value of the <sup>*</sup>up interest increases because of the direct value shift, group together all <sup>*</sup>up interests of the kind referred to in the relevant item that sustained the same increase in market value as the up interest because of the direct value shift.

<center>Back to Top</center>
 	If the up interest is issued at a discount, group together all up interests of the kind referred to in the relevant item that are issued at a discount of the same amount as the up interest because of the direct value shift.
 _Step 2._	The value shifted  to that group of <sup>*</sup>up interests from the <sup>*</sup>down interests referred to in the relevant item is the amount worked out using the formula:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1219.gif)</sub>
 	where:
 	_sum of the group increases or discounts_ means (as appropriate):

	(a)	the sum of the increases in market value of all <sup>*</sup>up interests in the group because of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift; or
 	(b)	the sum of the <sup>*</sup>discounts at which all <sup>*</sup>up interests in the group were issued because of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift.

	_total value of the direct value shift_ means:

	(a)	if the sum of the decreases in market value of all <sup>*</sup>down interests because of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift is equal to or greater than the sum of the increases in market value of all <sup>*</sup>up interests and all <sup>*</sup>discounts given because of the shift&#151;the sum of the decreases; or
 	(b)	if the sum of the decreases in market value of all down interests because of the direct value shift is less than the sum of the increases in market value of all up interests and all discounts given because of the shift&#151;the sum of the increases and discounts.

_Step 3_.	The uplift in the <sup>*</sup>adjustable value  of the <sup>*</sup>up interest under the relevant item is equal to:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1220.gif)</sub>

725-380  Decreases in adjustable value of down interests (with pre-shift losses)

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		Use the following method statement to work out the decrease in

<sup>*</sup>adjustable value of a <sup>*</sup>down interest under:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>item&#160;5 or 7 of the table in subsection 725-250(2); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>item&#160;3, 5 or 8 of the table in subsection 725-335(3).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Method statement_

_Step 1_.	Group together all <sup>*</sup>down interests of the kind referred to in the relevant item that:

	(a)	immediately before the <sup>*</sup>decrease time, had the same <sup>*</sup>adjustable value as the down interest; and
 	(b)	immediately before that time had the same market value as the down interest; and
 	(c)	sustained the same decrease in market value as the down interest because of the <sup>*</sup>direct value shift.

_Step 2._	Work out the value shifted from that group of <sup>*</sup>down interests to the <sup>*</sup>up interests referred to in the relevant item using the formula:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1221.gif)</sub>
 _Step 3_.	The decrease in <sup>*</sup>adjustable value of the <sup>*</sup>down interest under the relevant item is equal to:
 	<sub> ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1222.gif)</sub>

Division&#160;727&#151;Indirect value shifting affecting interests in companies and trusts, and arising from non-arm's length dealings

Table of Subdivisions

	Guide to Division&#160;727
 727-A	Scope of the indirect value shifting rules
 727-B	What is an indirect value shift
 727-C	Exclusions
 727-D	Working out the market value of economic benefits
 727-E	Key concepts
 727-F	Consequences of an indirect value shift
 727-G	The realisation time method
 727-H	The adjustable value method
 727-K	Reduction of loss on equity or loan interests realised before the IVS time
 727-L	Indirect value shift resulting from a direct value shift

Guide to Division&#160;727
 727-1  What this Division is about

If there is a net shift of value between 2 related entities because of a non-arm's length dealing, this Division:

	(a)	prevents losses from arising, because of the value shift, on 
<center>Back to Top</center>
 realisation of direct or indirect equity or loan interests in the losing entity; and
 	(b)	within limits, prevents gains from arising, because of the value shift, on realisation of direct or indirect equity or loan interests in the gaining entity.

However, it does so only for interests that are owned by entities involved in the value shift.

Table of sections 

727-5	What is an indirect value shift?
 727-10	How does this Division deal with indirect value shifts?
 727-15	When does an indirect value shift have consequences under this Division?
 727-25	Effect of this Division on realisations at a loss that occur before the nature or extent of an indirect value shift can be fully determined

727-5  What is an indirect value shift?

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An indirect value shift arises when there is a net shift of value from one

entity to another.

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Example:	Company A transfers property to company B in return for

a cash payment. If the market value of the property is $180 million but the

cash payment is only $50 million, there is a net shift of value from company A

to company B of $130 million.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>It is called _indirect_ because the transaction will have the

indirect effect of shifting value from equity or loan interests in the losing

entity to equity or loan interests in the gaining entity.</dd> 		This is because the net shift in value between the entities will usually _decrease_ the market value of interests in the losing entity and _increase_ the market value of interests in the gaining entity.  </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Example:	Assume that company C owns all the shares in company A

and company D owns all the shares in company B. The net shift of value from

company A to company B will reduce the value of company C's shares in company A

and increase the value of company D's shares in company B.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>It will also produce corresponding effects further up a chain of entities.

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Example:	Assume that company E owns all the shares in company C

and company D. The net shift of value from company A to company B will also

reduce the value of company E's shares in company C and increase the value of

its shares in company D.

 </dl></dl>

 ![A graphic exists here.](http://www.comlaw.gov.au/Details/C2004C01281/Html/9EF1056E86D3C5ACCA256F710056BC4B/$FILE/1223.gif)

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>This Division is _not_ concerned with the tax treatment of the net

shift in value between the entities at the bottom of the chains. Instead, it

deals with the effects on the market value of interests (both direct and

indirect) in those entities.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>An indirect value shift distorts the relationship between the market value of an equity or loan interest and its value for income tax purposes. When the interest is realised, this can produce an inappropriate loss for income tax purposes, or an inappropriate gain. </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Example:	If company E sold its shares in company C, the indirect

value shift could (apart from this Division) result in a loss for income tax

purposes. Company E could defer the corresponding gain on its shares in company

D by not selling these.

 </dl></dl>

727-10  How does this Division deal with indirect value shifts?

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>To prevent an inappropriate loss or gain from arising on realisation of an

interest, this Division reduces the amount of the loss or gain (realisation

time method). However, a choice can be made to adjust the interest's value for

income tax purposes in a way that takes account of the indirect value shift

(adjustable value method).</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>This Division does _not_ create taxing events giving rise to gains or losses. </dd> </dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

727-15  When does an indirect value shift have consequences under this Division?

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Indirect value shift is defined very broadly, but the application of this

Division is limited in various ways.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>The losing entity must be a company or trust (except a superannuation entity). However, the gaining entity can be any kind of entity, including an individual.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>This Division does _not_ apply if entities deal with each other at arm's length, or provide economic benefits in return for full market value.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>The losing entity and the gaining entity must be connected by having had the same _ultimate controller_. In the case of closely held entities, they may instead be connected by having had a high level of _common ownership_.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>The only interests affected are those owned by entities involved in the indirect value shift or by their associates.</dd> <dt>(6)</dt><dd>There are a range of exclusions, such as: </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>exclusions for minor indirect value shifts; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a series of rules designed to provide safe harbour treatment for common

transactions relating to services; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>anti-overlap provisions to prevent double-counting.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(7)</dt><dd>Rules of thumb are included to make it easier to determine the market

value of some kinds of economic benefits.</dd> <dt>(8)</dt><dd>To reduce compliance costs for: </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>entities in the Simplified Tax System; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>entities that meet the CGT small business net asset threshold ($5 million);

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

interests owned by those entities are not affected by this Division.

_\[The next section is sectionÂ 727-25.]_

727-25  Effect of this Division on realisations at a loss that occur before the nature or extent of an indirect value shift can be fully determined

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>To determine whether a scheme gives rise to an indirect value shift, it

must be possible to identify all the economic benefits under the scheme, and

the providers and recipients of those benefits.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>Before then, interests that might be affected by the scheme may be realised at a loss. Subdivision&#160;727-K contains special rules that apply if that happens. </dd> </dl></dl>

Subdivision&#160;727-A&#151;Scope of the indirect value shifting rules 

Table of sections 

727-95	Main object
 727-100	When an indirect value shift has consequences under this Division
 727-105	Ultimate controller test
 727-110	Common-ownership nexus test (if both losing and gaining entities are closely held)
 727-125	No consequences if losing entity is a superannuation entity

727-95  Main object

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		The main object of this Division is:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to prevent inappropriate losses from arising on the realisation of direct

or indirect equity or loan interests in an entity from which there has been a

net shift of value because of a non-arm's length dealing; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>to prevent inappropriate gains from arising on the realisation of direct

or indirect equity interests in the entity to which that value has been shifted;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

in cases where the 2 entities are related as set out in this Division.

727-100  When an indirect value shift has consequences under this Division

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		An <sup>*</sup>indirect value shift (see Subdivision&#160;727-B) has

consequences under this Division if, and only if:

 </dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the <sup>*</sup>losing entity is at the time of the indirect value shift a

company or trust (except one listed in section&#160;727-125 (about

superannuation entities)); and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in relation to either or both of the following:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the losing entity <sup>*</sup>providing one or more economic benefits to

the gaining entity <sup>*</sup>in connection with the <sup>*</sup>scheme from

which the indirect value shift results;</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the gaining entity providing one or more economic benefits to the losing

entity in connection with the scheme;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		the 2 entities are not dealing with each other at <sup>*</sup>arm's length;

and

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>either or both of sections&#160;727-105 and 727-110 are satisfied; and</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>no exclusion in Subdivision&#160;727-C applies.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	The consequences for direct and indirect interests in the

losing entity or in the gaining entity are set out in Subdivision&#160;727-F.

If those consequences are to be worked out using the realisation time method

(under Subdivision&#160;727-G), there are further exclusions for certain 95%

services indirect value shifts: see section&#160;727-700\. Note 2:	An indirect value shift does not have consequences for interests in the losing entity or gaining entity owned immediately before the IVS time by an entity that:  </dl></dl>

*	is eligible to be an STS taxpayer for each income year that includes any of the IVS period; or
 *	would satisfy the maximum net asset value test in section&#160;152-15 throughout the IVS period.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

	See subsection 727-470(2).

 </dl></dl>

727-105  Ultimate controller test

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		It must be the case that, at some time during the <sup>*</sup>IVS period:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the <sup>*</sup>losing entity and the <sup>*</sup>gaining entity have the

same <sup>*</sup>ultimate controller; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the ultimate controller of the losing entity is the same entity that was

the ultimate controller of the gaining entity at a different time during that

period; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the gaining entity is the ultimate controller of the losing entity; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the losing entity is the ultimate controller of the gaining entity.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

For the concept of _IVS period_, see section&#160;727-150.
 For the concept of _ultimate controller_, see section&#160;727-350.

727-110  Common-ownership nexus test (if both losing and gaining entities are closely held)

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Or, it must be the case that:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>at some time during the <sup>*</sup>IVS period, neither the

<sup>*</sup>losing entity nor the <sup>*</sup>gaining entity has 300 or more

members (in the case of a company) or 300 or more beneficiaries (in the case of

a trust); and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the losing entity and the gaining entity have a

<sup>*</sup>common-ownership nexus within the IVS period.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

For the concept of _IVS period_, see section&#160;727-150.
 For the concept of _common-ownership nexus_, see section&#160;727-400.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>Section&#160;124-810 (under which certain companies and trusts are not

regarded as having 300 or more members or beneficiaries) also applies for the

purposes of this Division.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>In addition, this Division applies to a <sup>*</sup>non-fixed trust as if it did not have 300 or more beneficiaries. </dd> </dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

727-125  No consequences if losing entity is a superannuation entity

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		An <sup>*</sup>indirect value shift has no consequences under this Division

if the <sup>*</sup>losing entity is one of these in relation to the income year

in which the indirect value shift happens:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a <sup>*</sup>complying superannuation fund; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a <sup>*</sup>non-complying superannuation fund; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a <sup>*</sup>complying approved deposit fund; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>a <sup>*</sup>non-complying approved deposit fund; or</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>a <sup>*</sup>pooled superannuation trust.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Subdivision&#160;727-B&#151;What is an indirect value shift 

Table of sections

727-150	How to determine whether a scheme results in an indirect value shift
 727-155	Providing economic benefits
 727-160	When an economic benefit is provided _in connection with_ a scheme
 727-165	Preventing double-counting of economic benefits

727-150  How to determine whether a scheme results in an indirect value shift

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A <sup>*</sup>scheme can result in one or more <sup>*</sup>indirect value

shifts only if one or more economic benefits have been, are being, or are to

be, <sup>*</sup>provided <sup>*</sup>in connection with the scheme.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>The question whether the <sup>*</sup>scheme has that result must be determined by reference to the facts and circumstances that exist at the earliest time (either when the scheme is entered into or later) when it is reasonable to conclude that: </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>all the economic benefits that have been, are being, or are to be,

<sup>*</sup>provided <sup>*</sup>in connection with the scheme can be

identified; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>for each of those economic benefits:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the entity that has provided, is providing, or is to provide, the economic

benefit can be identified; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the entity to which the economic benefit has been, is being, or is to be,

provided can be identified; and</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>if the economic benefit is to be provided&#151;those entities are in

existence, and the providing of the economic benefit is not contingent; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>there are no other economic benefits that are to be provided in connection

with the scheme if some contingency is met.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

That time is called the _IVS time_ for the scheme.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	In most cases, the IVS time will be at or soon after the

scheme is entered into. However, if:

 </dl></dl>

*	direct or indirect interests in a company or trust are realised at a loss  when the IVS time for the scheme has not yet happened (even if it never happens); and
 *	the company or trust has provided, is providing, is to provide, or might provide, economic benefits in connection with the scheme;

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

	there may be consequences for those interests similar to those

of an indirect value shift resulting from the scheme. See

Subdivision&#160;727-K.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The <sup>*</sup>scheme results in an _indirect value shift_

from one entity (the _losing entity_) to another entity (the

_gaining entity_) if the total market value of the one or more

economic benefits (the _greater benefits_) that the losing entity

has <sup>*</sup>provided, is providing, or is to provide, to the gaining entity

<sup>*</sup>in connection with the scheme exceeds:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the total market value of the one or more economic benefits (_lesser benefits_) that the gaining entity has provided, is providing, or is to

provide, to the losing entity in connection with the scheme; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>if there are no economic benefits covered by paragraph&#160;(a)&#151;nil.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

That excess is the amount of the indirect value shift.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>The market value of an economic benefit is to be determined as at the

earliest time when it is reasonable to conclude that:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the economic benefit can be identified; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>paragraph&#160;(2)(b) is satisfied for that benefit.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

For more rules affecting how the market value of an economic benefit is determined, see Subdivision&#160;727-D.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>Neither the <sup>*</sup>losing entity nor the <sup>*</sup>gaining entity

needs to be a party to the <sup>*</sup>scheme. A benefit can be provided by act

or omission.</dd> <dt>(6)</dt><dd>The indirect value shift happens at the <sup>*</sup>IVS time.</dd> <dt>(7)</dt><dd>The _IVS period_ for a <sup>*</sup>scheme starts immediately before the scheme is entered into and ends at the <sup>*</sup>IVS time.</dd> <dt>(8)</dt><dd>A contingency that is artificial, or is virtually certain to be met, is treated under this Division as if it had been met. </dd> </dl></dl>

727-155  Providing economic benefits

_Examples_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>These are some examples of an entity providing an economic benefit to

another entity:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the first entity pays an amount to the other entity (in this case the

market value of the benefit is the amount of the payment);</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the first entity provides an asset or services to the other entity;</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the first entity does something that creates an asset in the hands of the

other entity (for example, a company issues shares to its members);</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the first entity incurs a liability to the other entity, or increases a

liability it already owes to the other entity;</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>the first entity terminates all or part of a liability owed by the other

entity;</dd>

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>the first entity does something that increases the market value of an

asset that the other entity holds.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>These examples are not intended to limit the meaning of providing an

economic benefit.

</dd> </dl></dl>

_Things treated as economic benefits_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>This Division applies as if the ending of:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a <sup>*</sup>primary equity interest or <sup>*</sup>secondary equity

interest in an entity; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a right that the owner of a <sup>*</sup>primary equity interest or

<sup>*</sup>secondary equity interest in an entity has because of owning the

interest;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

were an economic benefit that the owner of the interest provides to that entity.

727-160  When an economic benefit is provided in connection with a scheme

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An economic benefit has been, is being, is to be, or might be,

<sup>*</sup>provided by an entity to another entity _in connection with_ a <sup>*</sup>scheme if, and only if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the benefit has been, is being, is to be, or might be, provided under the

scheme; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the providing of the benefit is reasonably attributable to:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>something that has been, is being, is to be, or might be, done or omitted

under the scheme (whether before, at the time of, or after, the providing of

the benefit) by an entity that is either of those entities or a third entity;

or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>2 or more such things.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>An entity referred to in paragraph&#160;(1)(b) need not be a party to the

<sup>*</sup>scheme. A benefit can be provided by act or omission.

</dd> </dl></dl>

727-165  Preventing double-counting of economic benefits

_Rights to have economic benefits provided_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If an economic benefit that has been, is being, is to be, or might be,

<sup>*</sup>provided as mentioned in subsection 727-150(3) or 727-855(1)

consists of a right to have economic benefits provided, that subsection applies

to the right but does not also apply to those economic benefits.

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Example:	Acme Ltd enters into an agreement with Paragon Pty Ltd

under which Acme is to provide services to Paragon over a 5 year period in

return for payments. 	Paragon's rights under the agreement are economic benefits that Acme provides to Paragon when the agreement is made. The services are economic benefits that Acme is to provide to Paragon. 	Because of this subsection, the market value of the rights is taken into account in working out whether there has been an indirect value shift, but the market value of the services is not.  </dl></dl>

_Effect of an economic benefit on interests in the entity to which it is provided_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If an economic benefit has been, is being, or is to be,

<sup>*</sup>provided to an entity, then, for the purposes of subsection

727-150(3) or 727-855(1), disregard an economic benefit to the extent that:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>it consists of an increase in the market value of:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>an <sup>*</sup>equity or loan interest in the entity; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>an <sup>*</sup>indirect equity or loan interest in the entity; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the increase is reasonably attributable to the first-mentioned benefit.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Subdivision&#160;727-C&#151;Exclusions
 Guide to Subdivision&#160;727-C
 727-200  What this Subdivision is about

Some indirect value shifts do not have consequences under this Division.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	If the consequences of an indirect value shift are to be

worked out using the realisation time method (under Subdivision&#160;727-G),

there are further exclusions for certain 95% services indirect value shifts:

see section&#160;727-700\. Note 2:	For cases where there may be both a direct value shift and an indirect value shift, see Subdivision&#160;727-L.  </dl></dl>

General
 727-215  Amount does not exceed $50,000

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An <sup>*</sup>indirect value shift does not have consequences under this

Division if the amount of it does not exceed $50,000.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>However, subsection&#160;(1) does not apply to an <sup>*</sup>indirect value shift (and is taken never to have applied to it) if: </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>before, at the same time as, or after it, another indirect value shift

happens for which the same entity is the losing entity as for the first

indirect value shift; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>having regard to all relevant circumstances, it is reasonable to conclude

that the sole or main reason why one of the indirect value shifts happened

under a different <sup>*</sup>scheme from the other was so that its amount

would not exceed $50,000.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

727-220  Disposal of asset at cost, or at undervalue if full value is not reflected in adjustable values of equity or loan interests in the losing entity

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An <sup>*</sup>indirect value shift does not have consequences under this

Division if the conditions in this section are met.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>The <sup>*</sup>greater benefits must consist entirely of: </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the <sup>*</sup>losing entity transferring a <sup>*</sup>CGT asset to the

<sup>*</sup>gaining entity; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a right to have the losing entity transfer an asset to the gaining entity.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>There must be <sup>*</sup>lesser benefits and, as at the <sup>*</sup>IVS

time, the total market value of the lesser benefits must not be less than the

greatest of these amounts:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the asset's <sup>*</sup>cost base at that time;</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the asset's cost;</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the asset's market value immediately before the most recent time (if any),

since the <sup>*</sup>losing entity <sup>*</sup>acquired the asset, when an

<sup>*</sup>affected owner has acquired:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a <sup>*</sup>primary equity interest in the losing entity; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>an <sup>*</sup>indirect primary equity interest in the losing entity.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>A <sup>*</sup>primary equity interest in an entity is an _indirect primary equity interest_ in another entity if, and only if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the first entity owns a primary equity interest in the other entity; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the first entity owns a primary equity interest that is an indirect

primary equity interest in the other entity because of one or more other

applications of this subsection.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_\[The next section is sectionÂ 727-230.]_

<center>Back to Top</center>

Indirect value shifts involving services
 727-230  Services provided by losing entity to gaining entity for at least their direct cost

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		An <sup>*</sup>indirect value shift does not have consequences under this

Division if:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to the extent of at least 95% of their total market value, the

<sup>*</sup>greater benefits consist entirely of:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a right to have services that are covered by section&#160;727-240 provided

directly by the losing entity to the gaining entity; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>services that are covered by section&#160;727-240 and have been, are

being, or are to be, so provided;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		or both; and

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>there are <sup>*</sup>lesser benefits and, as at the <sup>*</sup>IVS time,

the total market value of the lesser benefits is not less than the total of:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the present value of the direct cost to the losing entity of providing the

services; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the present value of a reasonable allocation of the total direct cost to

the losing entity of providing services that include the first-mentioned

services (so far as it is not already covered by subparagraph&#160;(i)).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

To work out the costs and present values referred to in paragraph&#160;(b),
see section&#160;727-245.

727-235  Services provided by gaining entity to losing entity for no more than a commercially realistic price

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An <sup>*</sup>indirect value shift does not have consequences under this

Division if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>there are <sup>*</sup>lesser benefits and, to the extent of at least 95%

of their total market value, the lesser benefits consist entirely of:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a right to have services that are covered by section&#160;727-240 provided

directly by the gaining entity to the losing entity; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>services that are covered by section&#160;727-240 and have been, are

being, or are to be, so provided;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		or both; and

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>as at the <sup>*</sup>IVS time, the total market value of the greater

benefits is not more than the total of:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the present value of the direct cost to the gaining entity of providing

the services; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the present value of a reasonable allocation of the total direct cost to

the gaining entity of providing services that include the first-mentioned

services (so far as it is not already covered by subparagraph&#160;(i)); and</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>the present value of a reasonable allocation of the indirect cost to the

gaining entity of providing the first-mentioned services; and</dd>

<dt>(iv)</dt><dd>the mark-up worked out under subsection&#160;(2) or (3) of this section.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

To work out the costs and present values referred to in paragraph&#160;(1)(b),
see section&#160;727-245.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If it is reasonable to estimate that an entity providing the same quantity

of services of the same kind in the same market would charge for them on the

basis of a particular percentage mark-up, or on the basis of a percentage

mark-up within a particular range, the mark-up for the purposes of

subparagraph&#160;(1)(b)(iv) is:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

*	the total of the respective present values of the costs mentioned in subparagraphs&#160;(1)(b)(i), (ii) and (iii);

multiplied by:

*	that percentage mark-up, or the highest percentage in that range.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>Otherwise, the mark-up for the purposes of subparagraph&#160;(1)(b)(iv) is

10% of the total of the respective present values of the costs mentioned in

subparagraphs&#160;(1)(b)(i), (ii) and (iii).

</dd> </dl></dl>

727-240  What services certain provisions apply to

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Sections&#160;727-230, 727-235, 727-700 and 727-725 apply only to services

consisting of:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>doing work (including professional work and giving professional advice or

any other kind of advice); or

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Note:	Examples include accounting or legal services; advertising services and financial management services.

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>providing (including allowing use of) facilities for entertainment,

recreation or instruction; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>leasing, renting, hiring, or allowing the use of, any asset; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>packaging, transporting or storing any property; or</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>providing insurance; or</dd>

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>services provided, by a banker to a customer, in the course of the banker

carrying on the business of banking; or</dd>

<dt>(g)</dt><dd>lending money or providing any other form of financial accommodation.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>It does not matter whether services covered by paragraph&#160;(1)(a) also

involve supplying property.

</dd> </dl></dl>

727-245  How to work out certain amounts for the purposes of sections&#160;727-230 and 727-235

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The costs mentioned in paragraph 727-230(b) or 727-235(1)(b) are to be

worked out:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>in accordance with generally accepted accounting practices; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>to the extent that the services are to be provided in the future, on the

basis of a reasonable estimate of those costs.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>To avoid doubt, the direct cost or indirect cost mentioned in paragraph

727-230(b) or 727-235(1)(b) does _not_ include:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to the extent that the services consist of or include lending money or

providing any other form of financial accommodation&#151;the amount of the loan or

other accommodation; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>to the extent that the services consist of or include leasing, renting,

hiring, or allowing the use of, any asset:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the cost of acquiring the asset; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the cost of acquiring an interest in, or right in respect of, the asset

in order to provide the services.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Example:	Acme Ltd is the holding company of Group Financier Pty

Ltd. Group Financier Pty Ltd borrows $20 million at 7% per annum, and on lends

it to other subsidiaries of Acme Ltd at 8% per annum. 	The $20 million does not form part of Group Financier Pty Ltd's direct cost of the services it provides to the other subsidiaries in the form of the on lending. However, the 7% interest that Group Financier Pty Ltd pays on the $20 million does form part of that direct cost.  </dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The present values mentioned in paragraph 727-230(b) or 727-235(1)(b) are

to be worked out using a discount rate equal to the rate that, for the purposes

of section&#160;109N of _Income Tax Assessment Act 1936_, is the benchmark

interest rate for the income year in which the <sup>*</sup>IVS time occurs.

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	That section is about distributions to entities connected

with a private company.

 </dl></dl>

Anti-overlap provisions
 727-250  Distribution by an entity to a member or beneficiary

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An <sup>*</sup>indirect value shift does not have consequences under this

Division if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the <sup>*</sup>greater benefits consist entirely of:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a distribution of income or capital that the <sup>*</sup>losing entity

makes to the <sup>*</sup>gaining entity; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>a right to a distribution of income or capital that the losing entity is

to make to the gaining entity;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		because the gaining entity holds <sup>*</sup>primary equity interests in the

losing entity; and

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>either:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>an amount covered by one or more of subsections&#160;(2), (3) and (4);

or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the total of 2 or more such amounts;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		equals or exceeds the amount of the distribution.

</dl></dl></dl>

_Conditions_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>This subsection covers an amount that the assessable income or exempt

income of the gaining entity for any income year includes because of the

distribution or right.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>This subsection covers an amount by which the <sup>*</sup>cost base or <sup>*</sup>reduced cost base (or both) of some or all of the <sup>*</sup>primary equity interests referred to in subsection&#160;(1) changes because of the distribution or right.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>This subsection covers an amount that, because of the distribution or right, is taken into account: </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>under section&#160;116-20 in working out the <sup>*</sup>capital proceeds

of a <sup>*</sup>CGT event that happens during any income year to some or all

of the <sup>*</sup>primary equity interests referred to in subsection&#160;(1);

or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in working out a <sup>*</sup>capital gain that an entity makes from CGT

event E4 or G1 happening during any income year to some or all of those primary

equity interests; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>in working out whether a loss or gain is <sup>*</sup>realised for income

tax purposes by a <sup>*</sup>realisation event that happens to some or all of

those primary equity interests (in their character as <sup>*</sup>trading stock

or <sup>*</sup>revenue assets).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Application of section to deemed dividend_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>If a <sup>*</sup>corporate tax entity makes a <sup>*</sup>distribution

that is not otherwise a distribution of income or capital, this section applies

as if the distribution were a distribution of income or capital the entity made.

</dd> </dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Subsection&#160;(5) extends this section to cover something

that is taken to be a dividend paid by a company. Compare item&#160;1 of the

table in subsection 960-120(1).

 </dl></dl>

_\[The next section is sectionÂ 727-260.]_

Miscellaneous
 727-260  Shift down a wholly-owned chain of entities

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An <sup>*</sup>indirect value shift does not have consequences under this

Division if the <sup>*</sup>gaining entity is a <sup>*</sup>wholly-owned

subsidiary of the <sup>*</sup>losing entity throughout the <sup>*</sup>IVS

period.

</dd> </dl></dl>

_Exception: impact on market value of primary loan interest_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>However, subsection&#160;(1) does not apply if the <sup>*</sup>indirect

value shift has produced a <sup>*</sup>disaggregated attributable decrease, in

the market value of an <sup>*</sup>affected interest in the <sup>*</sup>losing

entity that is also a <sup>*</sup>primary loan interest in an entity covered by

subsection&#160;(3), for the owner of the interest.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>This subsection covers: </dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the <sup>*</sup>losing entity; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>an entity that owns <sup>*</sup>primary equity interests in an entity that

this subsection covers because of one or more previous applications of it.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Subdivision&#160;727-D&#151;Working out the market value of economic benefits 

Table of sections

727-300	What the rules in this Subdivision are for
 727-315	Transfer, for its adjustable value, of depreciating asset acquired for less than $1,500,000

727-300  What the rules in this Subdivision are for

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		This Subdivision is used in determining whether there has been an

<sup>*</sup>indirect value shift and, if so:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>whether it has consequences under this Division; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>if it does, the amount of it.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_\[The next section is sectionÂ 727-315.]_

727-315  Transfer, for its adjustable value, of depreciating asset acquired for less than $1,500,000

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>This Division applies to an economic benefit consisting of:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an entity transferring to another entity a <sup>*</sup>depreciating asset

(except a building or structure) for which the transferring entity has deducted

or can deduct an amount under Division&#160;40; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a right to have an entity transfer such a depreciating asset to another

entity;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

as if the economic benefit's market value were equal to the greater (the _residual value_) of:

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the asset's <sup>*</sup>adjustable value at the time when the economic

benefit was or is <sup>*</sup>provided; and</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the value assigned to the asset at that time in the transferring entity's

books;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

but only if:

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>as at that time, the <sup>*</sup>cost of the unit to the transferring

entity is less than $1,500,000; and</dd>

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>it is reasonable for the transferring entity to conclude that the unit's

actual market value at that time was, is, or will be, not less than 80%, and

not more than 120%, of the residual value; and</dd>

<dt>(g)</dt><dd>both the transferring entity and the other entity choose to have the

market value of that economic benefit treated as being equal to the residual

value.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>each of 2 or more economic benefits of the kind mentioned in

subsection&#160;(1) has been, is being, is to be, or might be, provided by the

same transferring entity, to the same other entity, <sup>*</sup>in connection

with the same <sup>*</sup>scheme; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>it is reasonable for the transferring entity to conclude that the total of

the <sup>*</sup>depreciating assets' actual market values at the respective

times when the economic benefits were or are <sup>*</sup>provided was, is, or

will be, not less than 80%, and not more than 120%, of the total of their

respective residual values under subsection&#160;(1);

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

paragraph&#160;(1)(f) is taken to be satisfied for each of the economic benefits.

Subdivision&#160;727-E&#151;Key concepts 

Table of sections

Ultimate controller

727-350	_Ultimate controller_
 727-355	_Control (for value shifting purposes)_ of a company
 727-360	_Control (for value shifting purposes)_ of a fixed trust
 727-365	_Control (for value shifting purposes)_ of a non-fixed trust
 727-370	Preventing double counting for percentage stake tests
 727-375	Tests in this Subdivision are exhaustive

Common-ownership nexus and ultimate stake of a particular percentage

727-400	When 2 entities have a common-ownership nexus within a period
 727-405	_Ultimate stake_ of a particular percentage in a company
 727-410	_Ultimate stake_ of a particular percentage in a fixed trust
 727-415	Rules for tracing

Ultimate controller
 727-350  Ultimate controller

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		An entity is an _ultimate controller_ of another entity if, and

only if:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the first entity <sup>*</sup>controls (for value shifting purposes) the

other entity; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>there is no entity that controls (for value shifting purposes) both the

first entity and the other entity.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

727-355  Control (for value shifting purposes) of a company

_50% stake test_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An entity _controls (for value shifting purposes)_ a company

if the entity, or the entity and its <sup>*</sup>associates between them:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>can exercise, or can control the exercise of, at least 50% of the voting

power in the company (either directly, or indirectly through one or more

interposed entities); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>have the right to receive (either directly, or indirectly through one or

more interposed entities) at least 50% of any dividends that the company may

pay; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>have the right to receive for (either directly, or indirectly through one

or more interposed entities) at least 50% of any distribution of capital of the

company.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_40% stake test_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>An entity also _controls (for value shifting purposes)_ a

company if the entity, or the entity and its <sup>*</sup>associates between

them:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>can exercise, or can control the exercise of, at least 40% of the voting

power in the company (either directly, or indirectly through one or more

interposed entities); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>have the right to receive (either directly, or indirectly through one or

more interposed entities) at least 40% of any dividends that the company may

pay; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>have the right to receive (either directly, or indirectly through one or

more interposed entities) at least 40% of any distribution of capital of the

company;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

unless an entity (other than the first entity and its associates) either alone or together with its associates in fact controls the company.

_Actual control test_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>An entity also _controls (for value shifting purposes)_ a

company if the entity, either alone or together with its

<sup>*</sup>associates, in fact controls the company.

</dd> </dl></dl>

727-360  Control (for value shifting purposes) of a fixed trust

_40% stake test_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An entity _controls (for value shifting purposes)_ a

<sup>*</sup>fixed trust if the entity, or the entity and its

<sup>*</sup>associates between them, have the right to receive (either

directly, or indirectly through one or more interposed entities) at least 40%

of any distribution of trust income, or trust capital, to beneficiaries of the

trust.

</dd> </dl></dl>

_Other tests_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>An entity also _controls (for value shifting purposes)_ a

<sup>*</sup>fixed trust if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the entity, or an <sup>*</sup>associate of the entity, whether alone or

with other associates (the _relevant entity_), has the power to

obtain the beneficial enjoyment of the trust's capital or income (whether or

not by exercising its power of appointment or revocation, and whether with or

without another entity's consent); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the relevant entity is able to control the application of the trust's

capital or income in any manner (whether directly or indirectly); or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the relevant entity is able to do a thing mentioned in paragraph&#160;(a)

or (b) under a <sup>*</sup>scheme; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>a trustee of the trust is accustomed or is under an obligation (whether

formally or informally), or might reasonably be expected, to act in accordance

with the relevant entity's directions, instructions or wishes; or</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>the relevant entity is able to remove or appoint a trustee of the trust.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

727-365  Control (for value shifting purposes) of a non-fixed trust

_Trustee tests_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An entity _controls (for value shifting purposes)_ a

<sup>*</sup>non-fixed trust if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the entity or an <sup>*</sup>associate of the entity is a trustee of the

trust; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the entity, or the entity and its <sup>*</sup>associates between them, can

remove or appoint the trustee, or one or more of the trustees, of the trust;

or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a trustee of the trust is accustomed to act, is under an obligation

(whether formally or informally) to act, or might reasonably be expected to

act, in accordance with the directions, instructions or wishes of:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the entity or an <sup>*</sup>associate of the entity; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>2 or more entities, at least one of which is the entity or an associate

of the entity.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

_Tests based on control of the trust income or capital_

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>An entity also _controls (for value shifting purposes)_ a

<sup>*</sup>non-fixed trust if the entity, or the entity and its

<sup>*</sup>associates between them:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>have the power to obtain the beneficial enjoyment of trust income or

capital; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>can control in any way at all, whether directly or indirectly, the

application of trust income or capital; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>can, under a <sup>*</sup>scheme, gain the enjoyment or control referred to

in paragraph&#160;(a) or (b).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>An entity also _controls (for value shifting purposes)_ a

<sup>*</sup>non-fixed trust if:

</dd> </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the entity, or any of its <sup>*</sup>associates, can benefit under the

trust otherwise than because of a <sup>*</sup>fixed entitlement to a share of

the income or capital of the trust; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>if the entity, or the entity and its <sup>*</sup>associates between them,

have the right to receive (either directly, or indirectly through one or more

interposed entities) at least 40% of any distribution of trust income, or trust

capital.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

727-370  Preventing double counting for percentage stake tests

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		If an interest giving an entity, or an entity and its <sup>*</sup>associates:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the ability to exercise, or control the exercise of, any of the voting

power in a company; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the right to receive dividends that a company may pay; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the right to receive a distribution of capital of a company; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the right to receive a distribution of trust income or trust capital;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

is both direct and indirect, and (apart from this section) would be counted more than once in applying subsection 727-355(1) or (2) or section&#160;727-360, only the direct interest is to be counted.

727-375  Tests in this Subdivision are exhaustive

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		An entity does not _control (for value shifting purposes)_ a

company or trust except as provided in this Subdivision.

 </dl></dl>

Common-ownership nexus and ultimate stake of a particular percentage
 727-400  When 2 entities have a common-ownership nexus within a period

and only if, they satisfy the test in any of the one or more items in the table

applicable to them.
